<div id="review_1928114238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1928114238" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36819318-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485843897p2/36819318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1928114238?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/36819318-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36819318-scott?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1928114238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6531887235741558309">I used to pick up hitchhikers. Alone and starved of conversation on long-distance trips I'd stop for anyone short of an obvious axe murderer. Most of the people I picked up were guys in their 20s - fit, healthy men who would have been perfect targets for the protagonist of <i>Under The Skin</i>.<br/><br/>In Michael Faber's novel a lone woman named Isserley cruises the backroads of Scotland, picking up healthy, muscular male hitchers. She chats awkwardly with her new passengers, determining their health, their le</span>
  <span id="freeText6531887235741558309" style="display:none">I used to pick up hitchhikers. Alone and starved of conversation on long-distance trips I'd stop for anyone short of an obvious axe murderer. Most of the people I picked up were guys in their 20s - fit, healthy men who would have been perfect targets for the protagonist of <i>Under The Skin</i>.<br /><br />In Michael Faber's novel a lone woman named Isserley cruises the backroads of Scotland, picking up healthy, muscular male hitchers. She chats awkwardly with her new passengers, determining their health, their level of connectedness to their friends, their family and society. Then, with the flick of a switch on her steering column she sedates them and delivers them to a mysterious backwoods farm.<br /><br />Isserley’s days are spent driving, her nights trying to sleep through the torment her surgically altered body inflicts upon her. And the surgeries that have left her so pained were profoundly altering. Isserley is not a normal woman, and the things done to her so she can pass as a regular person have left her a mess of physical and psychological scars. <br /><br />This is a suspenseful story, filled with tantalising mysteries that will pull you through the novel like a jet-skier behind a boat. Why is Isserley abducting people? What happens to them on the farm? Who, or what exactly is our protagonist? <i>Under the Skin</i> slowly reveals the answers to these questions and I stayed up late with this book, caught up in Isserley's pained and conflicted life to the point where the novel consumed my thoughts all the following day. <br /><br />This isn't a book for the easily triggered. There is genuine horror in what is revealed. Some of the darker stuff has lodged in my mind - a disturbing mental burr in my psyche that I can’t quite pluck free - and I find myself involuntarily recalling it while reading other books. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Without going into too much spoiler-y detail, there are echoes in this novel of Peter Jackson's cult splatter film <i>Bad Taste</i> (a classic low budget 80s film in which Aliens harvest humans to make intergalactic food chain burger patties) in <i>Under the Skin</i>, although Faber’s story is the better one, with less gore and a great deal more heart.<br /><br /><i>Under the Skin</i> reads as a novel-length allegory of the cruelties inherent in the production and consumption of meat. The abducted hitchers are neutered, their tongues are removed, and then they are fattened in an underground feedlot prior to their slaughter for meat. The setting of these events- a farm – hammers home the intended message. At numerous points in the narrative Faber led me to reflect on the convenient justifications our society makes for the enslavement, mutilation and killing of animals for food, although I must confess that my own vegetarianism may have something to do with this interpretation.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />My only real gripe is that, in the early parts of the book at least, Faber pulls the rather tired trick of deliberately obscuring the appearances of his characters (or at least, parts of them) by simply not giving any details about how they look, when any observer on the scene would see them quite clearly. While this increases the sense of mystery it felt a little artificial. <br /><br />This annoyance aside <i>under the Skin</i> is a standout novel - a thoughtful, poignant and sad story with a strong message. It left me with a lot to think about, and I while I'm still happy to pick up hitchhikers I'm now doubly sure that I'll never risk thumbing rides myself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6531887235741558309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780156011600" href="/book/show/296355.Under_the_Skin">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K.D. by: </span>
      1001 Books You Must Read Before You Die (2006-2010)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=1001-core">1001-core</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=guy-lit">guy-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153514818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8556586493182266875">Surprisingly good. The book will keep you turning the pages because of the slow tease. In the end, I was expecting something like <i>The Silence of the Lambs</i> but Faber probably anticipated it and he brought me to a place I've never been before. That's despite that I already have 700+ books in different genres in my read folder. Definitely my first time to have encountered and read something like this.<br/><br/>It is a story of a pickup lady named <b>Isserly.</b> She drives back and forth in a Scottish highway looki</span>
  <span id="freeText8556586493182266875" style="display:none">Surprisingly good. The book will keep you turning the pages because of the slow tease. In the end, I was expecting something like <i>The Silence of the Lambs</i> but Faber probably anticipated it and he brought me to a place I've never been before. That's despite that I already have 700+ books in different genres in my read folder. Definitely my first time to have encountered and read something like this.<br /><br />It is a story of a pickup lady named <b>Isserly.</b> She drives back and forth in a Scottish highway looking for beefy young hitchhiking men. When she sees one, she assesses him first by passing through them and when she is certain, she makes a U-turn and picks the young man up. Then... I will not go on as this is a highly <i>spoilable</i> book. I will not even dare to put a spoiler (hide/show) because I have friends here who does not know how to behave and they just click on them. Just trust me when I say that, if you are any of the following, you will love this book:<blockquote>(1) <i>A lover of good storytelling that uses slow-tease.</i> The reason why Isserly picks the beefy young men and what do "they" do with those men; <br /><br />(2) <i>Mystery/suspense/sci-fi/fantasy aficionados.</i> The twists are just not easy to predict so I just lumped all those genres in there so as not to reveal too much. What I am trying to say is that if you love one of these genres, there is something in this book for you.<br /><br />(3) <i>A writer who is interested on how to play with POVs.</i> The bulk of the book is told in Isserly's point of view but every time there is a hitchhiker who has just got in her car, the POV shifts to him and I just loved knowing what the young man thinks of Isserly. I did enjoy these parts.<br /><br />(4) <i>If you are a meat-loving person.</i> I had the same feeling while reading Douglas Adams' <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8695.The_Restaurant_at_the_End_of_the_Universe__Hitchhiker_s_Guide___2_" title="The Restaurant at the End of the Universe (Hitchhiker's Guide, #2) by Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">The Restaurant at the End of the Universe</a>. Remember the talking giraffe?</blockquote>I think I have to stop now. Otherwise, I will spoil your fun! One last note (so I can remember if someone asks): the title comes from <b>Amlis</b> saying "We're all the same <i>under the skin</i>" when Isserly says that she does not really doubt if there's much similarity between the way he and she (Isserly) live and breath. (p. 164). <br /><br />This is a proof that not all 1001 books are serious or literary. This one is just different. The variety is one of the reasons why I am sticking to that list. It provides me with an unbelievable breath and width when it comes to reading experience. Just great! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8556586493182266875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2508169-paquita-maria-sanchez?shelf=literature">literature</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer954653535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11930521589020736860">Annnnnd now I can see the movie, whose trailer is the reason I read this book in the first place. The whole book-to-screen experience should have some degree of order to it, even if nothing else does in life. Especially if nothing else does in life. Book first 4 eva! <br/><br/>On the film's trailer/synopsis/general promotion, just a couple of things: 1) There's a spoiler innit concerning the who-what of the main character that the book opted to slow-reveal, which creates this weird situation where the tra</span>
  <span id="freeText11930521589020736860" style="display:none">Annnnnd now I can see the movie, whose trailer is the reason I read this book in the first place. The whole book-to-screen experience should have some degree of order to it, even if nothing else does in life. Especially if nothing else does in life. Book first 4 eva! <br /><br />On the film's trailer/synopsis/general promotion, just a couple of things: 1) There's a spoiler innit concerning the who-what of the main character that the book opted to slow-reveal, which creates this weird situation where the trailer makes you want to see the movie which makes you want to read the book, while also ruining the book a little, a book which you (me) wouldn't even have known about had it not been for that book-spoilering trailer, so it's not that big of deal because it was kind of a necessary sacrifice in order to know about the trailer about the movie about the book, but still. Ya follow me? This is a wordy warning. 2) I guess you aren't playing when you say something is "loosely based on the novel." Vulgar, juvenile joke about how loose it is. That movie that I haven't even seen yet can't possibly be much like this book that I actually have read, just based on these imagery buzzwords: hotchick, cityscapes, sexyclothes, at-the-mall, out-in-public, seduction, lipstick, no-glasses, no-scars, normal-naked. &lt;---Not featured in this book. Isserly, our main ladymam, does/is/experiences none of these things. On the contrary, her profound social awkwardness and startling appearance, her total dependence on her prosthetic tits and only her prosthetic tits to lure in her prey are major contributors to her inherent creepiness, and to what creates the feeling of panicked claustrophobia in all the "doomed hitch-hikers in her car" scenes in what is otherwise a sort of "Taxicab Confessions from Purgatory" tale. Oh yeah, I am so actually talking about the book all the sudden. Betcha didn't see that coming.<br /><br />This novel moves along pretty swiftly for one so technically slow-paced. At times, the metaphors at play feel a little ham-fisted, or long-winded, or both. Slivers of clever here and there, a few really great, really disturbing scenes. The romantic sub-plot reads like sloppy afterthought. The ending feels like a cheat. The animal rights theme is as subtle as a 10 car pile-up. <br /><br />*** I liked it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13584259909251565734">This was the perfect book for reading on rainy Scottish highways last week. I’m so glad I decided at the last minute to bring it along on our trip to Wigtown.<br/><br/>Isserley drives along Highland roads picking up hitchhikers – but only the hunky males – to take back to her farm near the Moray Firth. It’s likely that you already know the setup of this even if you haven’t read it, perhaps from the buzz around the 2013 film version starring Scarlett Johansson. It must have been so difficult for the first </span>
  <span id="freeText13584259909251565734" style="display:none">This was the perfect book for reading on rainy Scottish highways last week. I’m so glad I decided at the last minute to bring it along on our trip to Wigtown.<br /><br />Isserley drives along Highland roads picking up hitchhikers – but only the hunky males – to take back to her farm near the Moray Firth. It’s likely that you already know the setup of this even if you haven’t read it, perhaps from the buzz around the 2013 film version starring Scarlett Johansson. It must have been so difficult for the first reviewers and interviewers to discuss the book without spoilers back in 2000. David Mitchell, in his introduction to my Canons series reprint, does an admirable job of suggesting the eeriness of the contents without giving anything significant away.<br /><br />Shelve this under science fiction, though it veers towards horror and then becomes a telling allegory. I knew the basic plot beforehand, but there were still some surprises awaiting me, and I was impressed with how Faber pulled it all off. Keep an eye open for how he uses the word “human.” This has a lot to say about compassion and dignity, and how despite our differences we are fundamentally the same “under the skin.”<br /><br /><b>An atmospheric line:</b> “The fields all around her house were shrouded in snow, with patches of dark earth poking through here and there as if the world were a rich fruit cake under cream.”<br /><br />Originally published on my blog, <a href="https://bookishbeck.wordpress.com/2018/04/09/a-trip-to-wigtown-scotlands-book-town/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookish Beck</a>.</span>

<div id="review_1688869336" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1688869336" />
    <a title="Es Summer " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15104379-es-summer"><img alt="Es Summer " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466450844p2/15104379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1688869336?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Es Summer " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Es Summer " href="/user/show/15104379-es-summer">Es Summer </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782112112" href="/book/show/21136265-under-the-skin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1688869336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6976001137070077294"><i>“ISSERLEY ALWAYS DROVE straight past a hitch-hiker when she first saw him, to give herself time to size him up. She was looking for big muscles: a hunk on legs. Puny, scrawny specimens were no use to her.” </i><br/><br/><b> *Minor spoilers* </b><br/><br/>Disturbing, strangely compelling and original: Under the Skin is unlike anything I have ever read before. <br/>The story follows, Isserley, a female driver who picks up hitchhikers for secret purposes. She needs a certain type of guy: big muscled, tall and fit. What her reason is </span>
  <span id="freeText6976001137070077294" style="display:none"><i>“ISSERLEY ALWAYS DROVE straight past a hitch-hiker when she first saw him, to give herself time to size him up. She was looking for big muscles: a hunk on legs. Puny, scrawny specimens were no use to her.” </i><br /><br /><b> *Minor spoilers* </b><br /><br />Disturbing, strangely compelling and original: Under the Skin is unlike anything I have ever read before. <br />The story follows, Isserley, a female driver who picks up hitchhikers for secret purposes. She needs a certain type of guy: big muscled, tall and fit. What her reason is of needing these guys remains a mystery for a long time. <br /><br />During the rides, Isserley observes the hitchhiker while they try to get to know each other. <br />We get an insight in the thoughts of the hitchhikers as well and that makes it very interesting. Especially since the hitchhikers are more busy ogling Isserley than seeing the threat she actually is for them. <br /><br /><i> “Most distracting of all, though, was not the threat of danger but the allure of beauty.” </i><br /><br />The roles are reversed in Under the Skin and the female driver is the creepy one. There is something darkly amusing about the fact that a small woman chooses the biggest guys she can find, she lures them in with her femininity and outer appearance with the purposes of harming them in the meantime. <br /><br />Isserley is utterly creepy and it is difficult to really understand her throughout the novel. <br />That made it harder to connect with her. <br />Although the creepiness of the main narrator provided a grimy atmosphere, sometimes it dragged on a bit. The story had a very slow built-up and I wished for more action. <br /><br />Nevertheless, it was an interesting read and I would recommend it to horror lovers.<br /><br />3 stars.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6976001137070077294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_83321366" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83321366" />
    <a title="Agnieszka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2446508-agnieszka"><img alt="Agnieszka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371835955p2/2446508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83321366?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Agnieszka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Agnieszka" href="/user/show/2446508-agnieszka">Agnieszka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 0156011" href="/book/show/296213.Under_the_Skin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2446508-agnieszka?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2446508-agnieszka?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2446508-agnieszka?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2446508-agnieszka?shelf=1001-books">1001-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2446508-agnieszka?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83321366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9392684649140099674"><br/>It's an uncanny novel. Although it starts out as a classic thriller, Faber from first pages is playing with readers and misleading them. Repeating for The Times <i> here nothing is what it seems </i> and you become more and more disoriented, for this book is nothing like you had ever read before. At the same time engaging and repulsive. Unsettling. Disturbing.<br/><br/><br/>I'm not sure what I expected but was absolutely suprised. Faber consistently builds tension and leads us out of the atmosphere of horror in total</span>
  <span id="freeText9392684649140099674" style="display:none"><br />It's an uncanny novel. Although it starts out as a classic thriller, Faber from first pages is playing with readers and misleading them. Repeating for The Times <i> here nothing is what it seems </i> and you become more and more disoriented, for this book is nothing like you had ever read before. At the same time engaging and repulsive. Unsettling. Disturbing.<br /><br /><br />I'm not sure what I expected but was absolutely suprised. Faber consistently builds tension and leads us out of the atmosphere of horror in total fantasy, mixes so many genres and then serves extraordinary dish, neither thriller nor a crime story, nor science fiction. And finally leaves us with clear message that, after all, we are all the same under the skin.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9392684649140099674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7531217362168534695">I thought I knew what to expect, having seen (and enjoyed) the movie. But the book is entirely different, taking the story of this lone woman who picks up exclusively male hitchhikers in very creepy, bizarre and surprising directions. Faber does a good job at slowly lowering the curtain into Isserley’s life and motivations... but the less said about these, the better: so much of the fun is in the revelation. <i>Under the Skin</i> certainly has its weak points, but overall I found it so strange, unexpec</span>
  <span id="freeText7531217362168534695" style="display:none">I thought I knew what to expect, having seen (and enjoyed) the movie. But the book is entirely different, taking the story of this lone woman who picks up exclusively male hitchhikers in very creepy, bizarre and surprising directions. Faber does a good job at slowly lowering the curtain into Isserley’s life and motivations... but the less said about these, the better: so much of the fun is in the revelation. <i>Under the Skin</i> certainly has its weak points, but overall I found it so strange, unexpected and original, and the grotesque spectacle so compelling, that any faults were easy to overlook, and it was a pleasure to be picked up and taken along for the ride.</span>

<div id="review_1010280433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1010280433" />
    <a title="Leonard Gaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27098959-leonard-gaya"><img alt="Leonard Gaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442984307p2/27098959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1010280433?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leonard Gaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leonard Gaya" href="/user/show/27098959-leonard-gaya">Leonard Gaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8180719-under-the-skin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1010280433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1629287023348295299">I have been drawn to this book after watching the striking film, inspired by Faber’s novel and starring Scarlett Johansson. My account of the book is based on my reading half of it only. I have to admit that it just jumped out of my hands.<br/><br/>This book is a very unsettling, even sickening one. The story is rather casual at first, eventually horrifying: a young woman, who drives around in the Scottish Highlands, takes hunky hitch-hikers in her car and, after a short interview, decides whether to take</span>
  <span id="freeText1629287023348295299" style="display:none">I have been drawn to this book after watching the striking film, inspired by Faber’s novel and starring Scarlett Johansson. My account of the book is based on my reading half of it only. I have to admit that it just jumped out of my hands.<br /><br />This book is a very unsettling, even sickening one. The story is rather casual at first, eventually horrifying: a young woman, who drives around in the Scottish Highlands, takes hunky hitch-hikers in her car and, after a short interview, decides whether to take them out or let them go. We later discover that she is of an alien race and that her victims are drugged and submitted to some sort of force-feeding in a remote farm. The result is described in a rather explicit way: “The thought of a shaved, castrated, fattened, intestinally modified, chemically purified vodsel turning up at a police station or a hospital was a nightmare made flesh.” This premise is atrocious enough not to delve further into it.<br /><br />This literary nightmare made me think of some of Poe’s imaginations (the Antarctic race discovered by the sailors at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/766869.The_Narrative_of_Arthur_Gordon_Pym_of_Nantucket" title="The Narrative of Arthur Gordon Pym of Nantucket by Edgar Allan Poe" rel="nofollow noopener">The Narrative of Arthur Gordon Pym</a>). It is an inversion of sorts of the classic fairy tale theme Girl-eaten-by-Wolf. It also carries some distant echo of the mythical Valkyries, who retrieved heroes from the battlefield.<br /><br />Faber’s style is rousing in some strange way: the thoughts, the details of the girl's day-to-day life are described with an almost surgical fastidiousness. Each of the male characters she encounters has their distinct personality, accent, perception, inner monologue. The suspense is vivid, at least until it reaches the repulsive imagery of human livestock farming. Once the horror is revealed, the plot starts to go round and round in circles.<br /><br />The element of sexual drive is not as pervasive as in Johansson’s movie. But somehow, and in a more abstract, less matter-of-fact fashion, the film conveys an even subtler and higher horror than the novel.<br /><br /><i>Edit</i>: The influence of H. G. Wells’ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2493.The_Time_Machine" title="The Time Machine by H.G. Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">The Time Machine</a> and the dynamic between the Eloi and the Morlocks is quite obvious as well in Faber’s novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1629287023348295299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel (TheShadesofOrange)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel (TheShadesofOrange)" href="/user/show/7487619-rachel-theshadesoforange">Rachel (TheShadesofOrange)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7487619-rachel-theshadesoforange?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2696312872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12607064116973100746"><b>5.0 Stars<br/>One of the weirdest stories I have read. Ever. <br/>Video Review: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/Vu4nIERHIeI'>https://youtu.be/Vu4nIERHIeI</a> </b><br/><br/>From the synopsis, I went into this book with preconceived ideas that ended up being completely wrong. Initially, I expected a fun little thriller, but I quickly realized that this was something else. Thankfully, I loved that “something else”.<br/><br/>Blending together elements of horror, suspense and speculative fiction, this is the kind of book that blurs the lines between genres. First and foremost, this</span>
  <span id="freeText12607064116973100746" style="display:none"><b>5.0 Stars<br />One of the weirdest stories I have read. Ever. <br />Video Review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/Vu4nIERHIeI">https://youtu.be/Vu4nIERHIeI</a> </b><br /><br />From the synopsis, I went into this book with preconceived ideas that ended up being completely wrong. Initially, I expected a fun little thriller, but I quickly realized that this was something else. Thankfully, I loved that “something else”.<br /><br />Blending together elements of horror, suspense and speculative fiction, this is the kind of book that blurs the lines between genres. First and foremost, this is a literary story, but it’s one that will appeal to genre readers like myself. The writing and subsequent story were incredible to read. The author explored universal themes of humanity and morality without ever coming across as preachy. Admittedly, this book probably went over my head in places, but I still enjoyed the ride. I will absolutely be re-reading it in the future because I am certain I will get more out of it a second time.<br /><br />This book is incredibly hard to describe without giving away too much. However, if you are curious and willing to take a chance on a very different kind of story, then I would recommend trying this one for yourself. Who knows, if you are like me, you might find a new favourite.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12607064116973100746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_111681912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111681912" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/166376-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345482402p2/166376.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111681912?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/166376-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/166376-david?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111681912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12667555990835601401">This is one of the creepiest books I've read in years. It's also terrific - all kinds of props are due Michel Faber. He not only has the creative imagination to come up with such a bizarre, mesmerizing story; he also has the writing chops to execute it brilliantly. I can't think of any story I've read in the last several years that ratchets up the horror quotient so steadily, and so effectively. He's in total control throughout (hard to believe this was his first novel), writing in a style that'</span>
  <span id="freeText12667555990835601401" style="display:none">This is one of the creepiest books I've read in years. It's also terrific - all kinds of props are due Michel Faber. He not only has the creative imagination to come up with such a bizarre, mesmerizing story; he also has the writing chops to execute it brilliantly. I can't think of any story I've read in the last several years that ratchets up the horror quotient so steadily, and so effectively. He's in total control throughout (hard to believe this was his first novel), writing in a style that's fluid, lyrical in its description of the Scottish landscape, and totally creepy in the "you know something really, really bad is coming" way. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6877332" rel="nofollow noopener"> Paul's review </a> pretty much nails it:<br /><br />"you only find out bit by bit and it gets weirder until <b>you just can't stand it </b>".<br /><br />As usual, Paul gets it right. Read his review; I can't add a whole lot. The book isn't perfect; structurally, no ending could quite match the slow buildup of horror as the story progresses. But it's pretty damn good. I finished reading it about an hour ago - it's now 3am and I'm sitting in the dining room with every light in the apartment on, scared to go to bed. Even Hannibal Lecter didn't have this effect on me.<br /><br />So, yeah. Michel Faber brings the awesome here. Then there are his short stories, but that's material for a different review.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="12667555990835601401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3871556" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3871556" />
    <a title="Palmina Briggs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/169638-palmina-briggs"><img alt="Palmina Briggs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184643410p2/169638.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3871556?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Palmina Briggs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Palmina Briggs" href="/user/show/169638-palmina-briggs">Palmina Briggs</a>
      </span>

        rated it

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

                  <em>

<span id="freeTextContainer2570360969926799309">Completely captivating. To this day, this story haunts me. Takes place in Scotland and the main character is a female who picks up male hitchikers. What she does with them ... is well ... let's just say, I almost became a vegetarian, if it wasn't for being Croatian and meat-eating is a patriotic obligation. In an eery and out-of-this world way, this story forces you to examine how we treat animals.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16374678078829243451">A lonely stretch of road. A ribbon of slick tarmac stretching into the distant Scottish Highlands. There are few people around and every hitch hiker has to take their chances. After all what could possibly be dangerous about the young woman with the large eyes? <br/><br/>Beware of dark roads. Beware of the kindness of strangers. Evocative and well written, this is a difficult book to review without spewing forth spoiler after spoiler in a big frothing pool of spoiler vomit. Therefore I will not write too </span>
  <span id="freeText16374678078829243451" style="display:none">A lonely stretch of road. A ribbon of slick tarmac stretching into the distant Scottish Highlands. There are few people around and every hitch hiker has to take their chances. After all what could possibly be dangerous about the young woman with the large eyes? <br /><br />Beware of dark roads. Beware of the kindness of strangers. Evocative and well written, this is a difficult book to review without spewing forth spoiler after spoiler in a big frothing pool of spoiler vomit. Therefore I will not write too much more. And I feel a bit nauseous from describing pools of word vomit. It is clear from the start that something is very wrong with the woman in the car. The story is driven by the need to know her motivations, the reasoning behind the specific choice of prey and a desire to understand their ultimate fate. <br /><br />The story will have you evaluating how you decide what is a suitable food source and re-evaluating what it means to be human and a meat eater. You'll find yourself thinking a lot about whether or not cows have a sort of society that we're not aware of too. Cheerfully i'm a vegetarian so the meaty parts didn't bother me too much and the closest I ever get to a steak is to give it a friendly pat on the nose while it's still up and about and mooing its cheerful way around a nice green field. <br /><br />This is a surprise entry for the 1001 books list but also it proves the joy of the list. As well as providing a handy reference for the more conventional classic literature (Hardy, Austen, Bronte, Dickens and the rest of the usual suspects), it also throws the odd curve ball, this book being a case in point. Not something I'd have looked at twice without prompting but it was very, very good. Although how the author veered from this to the Crimson Petal and the White is a bit of a mystery.</span>

<div id="review_852398245" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/852398245" />
    <a title="Joe Valdez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez"><img alt="Joe Valdez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585885999p2/26876584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/852398245?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe Valdez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe Valdez" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez">Joe Valdez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780151006267" href="/book/show/829663.Under_the_Skin">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Hitchhikers, carnivores, lonely hearts</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26876584-joe-valdez?shelf=sci-fi-general">sci-fi-general</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer852398245&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer852398245" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12570323249402040951">I came to Michel Faber's <i>Under the Skin</i> after I went to see the elliptical, provocative and unsettling film adaptation starring Scarlet Johansson. With context and character names completely stripped from the movie, I was curious what a literal version of this story would be like. I got a lot of answers and a few more questions.<br/><br/>Stop reading unless you want the surprises spoiled.<br/><br/>The novel introduces a woman named Isserley driving a battered red Toyota Camry up and down the A9 in the Highlands of </span>
  <span id="freeText12570323249402040951" style="display:none">I came to Michel Faber's <i>Under the Skin</i> after I went to see the elliptical, provocative and unsettling film adaptation starring Scarlet Johansson. With context and character names completely stripped from the movie, I was curious what a literal version of this story would be like. I got a lot of answers and a few more questions.<br /><br />Stop reading unless you want the surprises spoiled.<br /><br />The novel introduces a woman named Isserley driving a battered red Toyota Camry up and down the A9 in the Highlands of Scotland. She's on the prowl for male hitchhikers, brawny men only, and never women. Isserley engages the hitchers in conversation, assessing what types of employment they have, whether they live in the area and whether they have a wife or girlfriend.<br /><br />Faber insinuates that Isserley might be cruising for sex, or possibly murder victims, until she sizes up a proper candidate and using a switch concealed in the Toyota's steering wheel, plunges two needles hidden in the passenger seat into the hitcher, drugging him. She returns to a farm compound where her co-workers await. They are not of this earth.<br /><br />Isserley has been surgically altered to resemble a "vodsel", an alien term for the crude inhabitants of Earth whose flesh, in the world of the "human beings" where Isserley is from, is consumed as a delicacy. An employee of the Vess Corporation, Isserley is in constant pain from her operation (one of the hitchers asks if she's been in a car accident). She lives on the farm with a manager who has also been altered, while the laborers who toil underground processing the vodsels walk on all fours, are covered in a pelt, have long necks, six fingers and powerful tails. <br /><br />Isserley keeps herself in a bitter mood, her only enjoyment coming from the trees, tides, snow or clouds of Earth, natural processes which have disappeared from her world. Her mood changes for the worse when farm receives a visit from Amlis Vess, the wayward son of the corporate honcho. Amlis believes eating flesh of an animal that breathes the same air they do is wrong and has a theory that vodsels possess a crude form of language. Isserley says nothing to confirm this. The longer she remains in her new body, the more she struggles with her own identity, unable to ever go home or make earth her new one.<br /><br /><i>Under the Skin</i> draws uneasy parallels between livestock farming and environmental decay, skillfully suggesting it might not be possible to have one without the other. The treatment of the "cattle" certainly stretches the limits of humane. The paragraphs revealing how the vodsels have their tongues and testicles removed, are shaved, artificially fattened over a month in pens and finally slaughtered are nightmarish. These revelations are nicely drawn out by Faber, who gives the book space rather than dumping information on the reader.<br /><br />I admired that Faber refused to force a Book of the Month plot onto the reader. No love interest for Isserley. No police detective on Isserley's trail. The lack of a plot does make the book feel like a novella padded out to novel length. I found myself skipping over paragraphs, wanting to get past the author's descriptions and fall into a story; that never really happens. I didn't find myself nearly as unsettled over Isserley's remorseless or the infinite unknown of her being as I did watching the movie. In many ways, she's not much different from a disgruntled mailman.<br /><br />That said, the last paragraph has a haunting finality that will be with me for a while. With a great deal of composure, Faber was able to stretch my imagination and make me feel something. Three and a half stars rounded up to four stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12570323249402040951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1635105232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1635105232" />
    <a title="Bill Khaemba" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41380936-bill-khaemba"><img alt="Bill Khaemba" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561102062p2/41380936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1635105232?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill Khaemba" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill Khaemba" href="/user/show/41380936-bill-khaemba">Bill Khaemba</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=thriller-suspense-crime-mystrey">thriller-suspense-crime-mystrey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=horror-scary">horror-scary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=highly-rated-books">highly-rated-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41380936-bill-khaemba?shelf=atmospheric-books">atmospheric-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1635105232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8040810801559071401"><b> This will haunt me for awhile, I need to go sit in a dark corner & contemplate 🙂 </b><br/><p>
  <em>
    <strong>
      "Most distracting of all, though, was not the threat of danger but the allure of beauty"
    </strong>
  </em>
</p><br/><p>In this speculative tale reminiscent of Atwood's The Handmaid's Tale we follow Isserley, a woman who is obsessed with picking up well-muscled hitchhikers on the backdrop of a Scotland Highway. Why she is picking them up and asking them personal questions, is a mystery that will reveal a dark side to this </p></span>
  <span id="freeText8040810801559071401" style="display:none"><b> This will haunt me for awhile, I need to go sit in a dark corner &amp; contemplate 🙂 </b><br><p>
  <em>
    <strong>
      "Most distracting of all, though, was not the threat of danger but the allure of beauty"
    </strong>
  </em>
</p><br><p>In this speculative tale reminiscent of Atwood's The Handmaid's Tale we follow Isserley, a woman who is obsessed with picking up well-muscled hitchhikers on the backdrop of a Scotland Highway. Why she is picking them up and asking them personal questions, is a mystery that will reveal a dark side to this simple act.</p><br><p>
  <em>
    <strong>“The word troubled her, though. ‘Indispensable.’ It was a word people tended to resort to when dispensability was in the air.</strong>
  </em>
</p><br><p>This was eerie, unsettling and downright fascinating one of those haunting tales that creep up on you as you flip the pages. For such a slim book (280 pages) <strong>Faber</strong> crammed so much and managed to seamlessly weave into the plot. I will vaguely speak about the overall story because I believe this is a story that one dives in blindly and just gets f*cked up.</p><br><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508341987i/24203681._SX540_.jpg" alt="Image result for Under the Skin illustrations" width="272" height="206" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br>The exploration of the main character's identity, her interactions with the male hitchhikers and her workmates opens up the discussion surrounding gender powerplay &amp; objectivism. Showcasing how uncomfortable she feels with all the masculinity surrounding her and losing herself in the process as she rarely encounters a female character in her work or day to day life. It was a topic that captures the feeling of isolation and addresses certain stereotypes. (Side Note: Trigger Warning for violent abuse)<br><br>Also, an underlying topic on animal breeding was done well, it had a twist that made me question my eating habits. This one of those that I could spend hours thinking about and the whole idea of placing the reader with this woman on a lonely highway felt personal and fascinating especially when a hitchhiker comes along.  Why it reminds me of the Handmaid's Tale was the story structure, the reader is slowly immersed into this disturbing world and the horrific scenes happening that shine the light on certain social issues.<br><br>Some of the small issues I had was the pacing, it felt a bit off towards the middle and at times I couldn't picture certain characters well but the overall experience was still worthwhile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8040810801559071401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1583088943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1583088943" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2242482-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326923603p2/2242482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1583088943?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/2242482-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2242482-david?shelf=big-white-square">big-white-square</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1583088943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer156189078394211490">I've thought about being a vegetarian ... one of my arguments has been how shameful it'll be when aliens land and see what we've done. "Yeah, for several centuries we've been breeding and breeding this living thing and now it looks like this. We've kept this one in a cage for its entire life. Now we're going to kill it and eat it. Sausage roll?" Yuck. Can you imagine how embarrassing it's going to be? <br/><br/>Fabulously, however, "Under the Skin" has aliens doing to us what we do to animals. <br/><br/>And it's ab</span>
  <span id="freeText156189078394211490" style="display:none">I've thought about being a vegetarian ... one of my arguments has been how shameful it'll be when aliens land and see what we've done. "Yeah, for several centuries we've been breeding and breeding this living thing and now it looks like this. We've kept this one in a cage for its entire life. Now we're going to kill it and eat it. Sausage roll?" Yuck. Can you imagine how embarrassing it's going to be? <br><br>Fabulously, however, "Under the Skin" has aliens doing to us what we do to animals. <br><br>And it's about relationships, gender, sex ... I couldn't stop reading.<br><br>I'd seen the film - and loved it, really loved it - and this is equally fabulous whilst being completely different. Great writing. And I think I've fallen in love with .... Isserley.<br><br>Weirdly, I couldn't stop imagining Amliss Vess as Chase from "Paw Patrol":<br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458502494i/18495601.png" width="500" height="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="156189078394211490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer7477676918009596088">Cypt, thank you for the rec!<br/><br/>Well, to be honest - this was not what I expected. Surprised in a good way and in awe how well it was written I swallowed this book as fast as it was possible. Not going to retell the plot, that would be an absolute and deadly (lol!) spoiler, the blurb is already more than enough. I'm not even going to put some of my tags, because that would be a total spoiler too. Prepare to have your feelings mixed and cheering for the wrong guy (and that might be so ambiguous at ti</span>
  <span id="freeText7477676918009596088" style="display:none">Cypt, thank you for the rec!<br /><br />Well, to be honest - this was not what I expected. Surprised in a good way and in awe how well it was written I swallowed this book as fast as it was possible. Not going to retell the plot, that would be an absolute and deadly (lol!) spoiler, the blurb is already more than enough. I'm not even going to put some of my tags, because that would be a total spoiler too. Prepare to have your feelings mixed and cheering for the wrong guy (and that might be so ambiguous at times). If it seems too dark to you - just take it as a metaphor.<br />I will only add that no matter how much disturbing and weird this was, it was also funny and very beautiful at times. Very unexpected book. I'll miss Isserly. Sometimes.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('b6Xf/WhixCU5w3eWyTpfYnsZoBGyP7yLYN01tUhBHEzr3w7RboSqGa9hHlNaWJG66uox6a7Gt1biHXHDQIZz5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rbh8+m0EGYh9T+1/EEpLLknhJyxO/K9Owx6wnNs19lgpwq3Wa+J3tOvthLqDKIX22BK21FIFpJNB3vTq0/KZ8g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2044356193390727887">Michel Faber (born 13 April 1960) is a Dutch writer of English-language fiction.<br/><br/>Faber was born in The Hague, The Netherlands. He and his parents emigrated to Australia in 1967. He attended primary and secondary school in the Melbourne suburbs of Boronia and Bayswater, then attended the University Of Melbourne, studying Dutch, Philosophy, Rhetoric, English Language (a course involving translation a</span>
  <span id="freeText2044356193390727887" style="display:none">Michel Faber (born 13 April 1960) is a Dutch writer of English-language fiction.<br /><br />Faber was born in The Hague, The Netherlands. He and his parents emigrated to Australia in 1967. He attended primary and secondary school in the Melbourne suburbs of Boronia and Bayswater, then attended the University Of Melbourne, studying Dutch, Philosophy, Rhetoric, English Language (a course involving translation and criticism of Anglo-Saxon and Middle English texts) and English Literature. He graduated in 1980. He worked as a cleaner and at various other casual jobs, before training as a nurse at Marrickville and Western Suburbs hospitals in Sydney. He nursed until the mid-1990s. In 1993 he, his second wife and family emigrated to Scotland, where they still reside.</span>
